            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwo96Ash7WNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0q409aT1HgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCrsLjE&amp;md5=d938be66a2a0948e3d2f589b803dbf76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201501527"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiang, X.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances and Prospects of Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiang, Xingde; Zhang, Kai; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">36</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5343-5364</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Na-ion batteries (SIBs) receive significant attention for electrochem. energy storage and conversion owing to their wide availability and the low cost of Na resources.  However, SIBs face challenges of low specific energy, short cycling life, and insufficient specific power, owing to the heavy mass and large radius of Na+ ions.  As an important component of SIBs, cathode materials have a significant effect on the SIB electrochem. performance.  The most recent advances and prospects of inorg. and org. cathode materials are summarized here.  Among current cathode materials, layered transition-metal oxides achieve high specific energies around 600 mW h g-1 owing to their high specific capacities of 180-220 mA h g-1 and their moderate operating potentials of 2.7-3.2 V (vs. Na+/Na).  Porous Na3V2(PO4)3/C nanomaterials exhibit excellent cycling performance with almost 100% retention over 1000 cycles owing to their robust structural framework.  Recent emerging cathode materials, such as amorphous NaFePO4 and pteridine derivs. show interesting electrochem. properties and attractive prospects for application in SIBs.  Future work should focus on strategies to enhance the overall performance of cathode materials in terms of specific energy, cycling life, and rate capability with cationic doping, anionic substitution, morphol. fabrication, and electrolyte matching.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRG1Bub04s8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0q409aT1HgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlCjur7N&amp;md5=6d0a96f9e9421c02a9f3b48744267752</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501727"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huang, Y. H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, W. X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, J.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Rich Na3+xV2-xNix(PO4)3/C for Sodium Ion Batteries: Controlling the Doping Site and Improving the Electrochemical Performances</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hui; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng; Ni, Qiao; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">27779-27787</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In order to get an element substituted into Na3V2(PO4)3/C in an appointed V site, the simple sol-gel method is used to design and prep. a series of Na-rich Na3+xV2-xNix(PO4)3/C (x = 0-0.07) compds.  To get a charge balance, the ratio of Na, V, and Ni would be changed if Ni goes into a different site.  Hence, ICP is applied to probe the real stoichiometry of the as-prepd. Na3+xV2-xNix(PO4)3/C (x = 0-0.07).  According to the Na/V ratio from the ICP result, it indicates that Ni2+ goes to a V site, and more Na+ will be introduced into the crystal to keep the charge balance.  In addn., the crystal structure changes are explored by XRD and Rietveld refinement, it is indicated from the results that Ni2+ doping does not destroy the lattice structure of Na3V2(PO4)3.  When applied as Na-storage material, the electrochem. property of all Ni2+ doped Na3+xV2-xNix(PO4)3/C composites have been significantly improved, esp. for the Na3.03V1.97Ni0.03(PO4)3/C sample.  For example, 107.1 mAh g-1 can be obtained at the first cycle; after 100 cycles, the capacity retention is as high as 95.5%.  Moreover, when charging/discharging at a higher rate of 5 C, the capacity still remains 88.9 mAh g-1, displaying good rate performance.  The good electrochem. performance is ascribed to the optimized morphol., stable crystal structure, and improved ionic cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQTZRMrirrTLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li0q409aT1HgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsFKmsLvN&amp;md5=e7562109537468250114c379df720cf5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b11848"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, L.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Sodium Ion Storage Behavior of P2-Type Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2 Synthesized via a Chelating Agent Assisted Route</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Ying; Zhao, Lixiang; Wu, Chuan; Li, Hui; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">From resource abundance and low cost, high capacity layered P2-type Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2 material is regarded as a potential cathode material for Na-ion batteries but suffers from its unstable structure during cycling.  P2-type Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2 layered materials were synthesized by a chelating agent assisted sol-gel method with NH3·H2O.  With the addn. of NH3·H2O and the control of the synthesis conditions, highly active material with a more stable structure and better electrochem. performance was obtained.  Also, the influences of structure changes during different voltage ranges (1.5-4.0 V and 1.5-4.3 V vs. Na+/Na) on the Na+ storage behavior was also evaluated and compared.  When being charged to 4.2 V, an OP4-type phase emerges, which can reduce the damage by the gilding of the MeO2 layers but leads to an unstable crystal structure.  For long-term cycling, it is preferred to cut off at 4.0 V rather than at 4.3 V.  For the optimized P2-type Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2 calcined at 900°, a discharge capacity of 92 mA h/g remains after 40 cycles in the voltage range of 1.5-4.0 V, and the Coulombic efficiency remains 100%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqEFOJ0dW4c4LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAOLbw9AdTDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xis1Ghug%253D%253D&amp;md5=58a1d0dd4859953759b23d8a3e32d4b8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600275"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ni, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyanion-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyanion-Type Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni Qiao; Bai Ying; Wu Feng; Wu Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1600275</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries, representative members of the post-lithium-battery club, are very attractive and promising for large-scale energy storage applications.  The increasing technological improvements in sodium-ion batteries (Na-ion batteries) are being driven by the demand for Na-based electrode materials that are resource-abundant, cost-effective, and long lasting.  Polyanion-type compounds are among the most promising electrode materials for Na-ion batteries due to their stability, safety, and suitable operating voltages.  The most representative polyanion-type electrode materials are Na3V2(PO4)3 and NaTi2(PO4)3 for Na-based cathode and anode materials, respectively.  Both show superior electrochemical properties and attractive prospects in terms of their development and application in Na-ion batteries.  Carbonophosphate Na3MnCO3PO4 and amorphous FePO4 have also recently emerged and are contributing to further developing the research scope of polyanion-type Na-ion batteries.  However, the typical low conductivity and relatively low capacity performance of such materials still restrict their development.  This paper presents a brief review of the research progress of polyanion-type electrode materials for Na-ion batteries, summarizing recent accomplishments, highlighting emerging strategies, and discussing the remaining challenges of such systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRzOrk04pyNfsjl5L8hwNX0fW6udTcc2eYJgreu74UnYrntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1cvgtVOitA%253D%253D&amp;md5=f4bc597b44df5e4e4c0b0a698c9a4d56</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.06.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, M. Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controllable Synthesis of High-Rate and Long Cycle-Life Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Controllable synthesis of high-rate and long cycle-life Na3V2(PO4)3 for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hui; Wu, Chuan; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng; Wang, Muzi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">326</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14-22</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Structural and morphol. control is an effective approach for improvement of electrochem. performance in rechargeable batteries.  In this paper, three different morphol. Na3V2(PO4)3 (irregular shaped, the porous sponge-like and plate like) were successfully prepd. through controlling the amt. of oxalic acid by a simple two-step redn. method.  It is found that the amt. of oxalic acid has vital impacts on the morphol. of Na3V2(PO4)3; moreover, the morphol. evolution and formation mechanism are proposed based on the reactions of different amt. of oxalic acid occurring in the two-step redn. process.  The excellent electrochem. performances of the porous sponge-like Na3V2(PO4)3 are attributed to the unique morphol.  The initial capacity of the porous sponge-like Na3V2(PO4)3 is 101.77 mAh g-1 at 30 C; after 700 cycles, it remains as high as 89.28 mAh g-1 with only 12% capacity loss.  When the c.d. increases to 50 C and 70 C, the capacity retentions of 81% after 600 cycles, and 92.5% after 500 cycles are achieved, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZ0c7dDo8aF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAOLbw9AdTDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFahsLfL&amp;md5=9626fd72dd5f1bb4fe2f2e57a7db522a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00277J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, X.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of Mg doping on the remarkably enhanced electrochemical performance of Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hui; Yu, Xiqian; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng; Wu, Chuan; Liu, Liang-Yu; Yang, Xiao-Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9578-9586</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2-xMgx(PO4)3/C composites with different Mg2+ doping contents (x = 0, 0.01, 0.03, 0.05, 0.07 and 0.1) were prepd. by a facile sol-gel method.  The doping effects on the crystal structure were investigated by XRD, XPS and EXAFS.  The results show that low dose doping of Mg2+ does not alter the structure of the material, and magnesium is successfully substituted for the vanadium site.  The Mg-doped Na3V2-xMgx(PO4)3/C composites exhibit significant improvements on the electrochem. performance in terms of the rate capability and cycle performance, esp. for the Na3V1.95Mg0.05(PO4)3/C.  For example, when the c.d. increased from 1 C to 30 C, the specific capacity only decreased from 112.5 to 94.2 mA h g-1 showing very good rate capability.  Moreover, even cycling at a high rate of 20 C, an excellent capacity retention of 81% is maintained from the initial value of 106.4 to 86.2 mA h g-1 at the 50th cycle.  Enhanced rate capability and cycle performance can be attributed to the optimized particle size, structural stability and enhanced ionic and electronic cond. induced by Mg doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqjzUp4E_iVMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAOLbw9AdTDA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVajurg%253D&amp;md5=9fc8cec833e02fc1b2a5323c30b9f106</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/admi.201500740"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bi, X.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Most P2-type layered oxides exhibit Na+/vacancy-ordered superstructures because of strong Na+-Na+ interaction in the alkali metal layer and charge ordering in the transition metal layer.  These superstructures evidenced by voltage plateaus in the electrochem. curves limit the Na+ ion transport kinetics and cycle performance in rechargeable batteries.  Here we show that such Na+/vacancy ordering can be avoided by choosing the transition metal ions with similar ionic radii and different redox potentials, for example, Cr3+ and Ti4+.  The designed P2-Na0.6[Cr0.6Ti0.4]O2 is completely Na+/vacancy-disordered at any sodium content and displays excellent rate capability and long cycle life.  A sym. sodium-ion battery using the same P2-Na0.6[Cr0.6Ti0.4]O2 electrode delivers 75% of the initial capacity at 12C rate.  Our contribution demonstrates that the approach of preventing Na+/vacancy ordering by breaking charge ordering in the transition metal layer opens a simple way to design disordered electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrlj5SkXA-GV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg4Ga2yHXOPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2ksrfJ&amp;md5=719e1ce8412c6a1d17ca3f1b29c3314e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acc.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljg4Ga2yHXOPA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/ijch.201400118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Development on Anodes for Na-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Isr.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Development on Anodes for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bommier, Clement; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Israel Journal of Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  New discoveries in anode materials for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) are highly necessary to achieve the goals of widespread applications, such as elec. vehicles (EVs) and grid-level energy storage.  Carbon-based materials are crit. for this task as they are inexpensive, abundant, and versatile.  They contain a plethora of structures and morphologies, ranging from highly ordered graphite or nanotubes to highly disordered amorphous carbon, thus making them very attractive for electrochem. energy storage.  This review attempts to cover past and recent progress in the development of carbon-based anode materials for NIBs.  To give a larger context, the article will briefly cover other anode materials for NIBs as well.  The aim of this paper is to provide a timely update for researchers currently involved in the resp. fields or to serve as a starting point for individuals who would like to gain a greater knowledge of new NIB anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQXhpe-bbd8rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljeqMG63hb4TA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVaqtbk%253D&amp;md5=c937a91d24c3ff50c8a97cb7302a09cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b00861"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hard Carbon Originated from Polyvinyl Chloride Nanofibers As High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bai, Ying; Wang, Zhen; Wu, Chuan; Xu, Rui; Wu, Feng; Liu, Yuanchang; Li, Hui; Li, Yu; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two types of hard carbon materials were synthesized by direct pyrolysis of com. polyvinyl chloride (PVC) particles and pyrolysis of PVC nanofibers at 600-800°, resp., where the nanofibers were prepd. by an electrospinning PVC precursors method.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Pursuing low-cost and high-performance anode materials is of great importance for developing practical sodium ion batteries.  In this work, mille-feuille shaped hard carbons derived from low-cost and environmentally friendly polyvinylpyrrolidone (PVP) nanofibres are fabricated via simple electrostatic spinning and followed by further pyrolysis at 800-1200 °C, as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-Surface-Area Hard Carbon Anode for Na-Ion Batteries via Graphene Oxide as a Dehydration Agent</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Bommier, Clement; Jian, Zelang; Li, Xin; Carter, Rich; Vail, Sean; Lu, Yuhao; Lee, Jong-Jan; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2626-2631</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries are emerging as one of the most promising energy storage technologies, particularly for grid-level applications.  Among anode candidate materials, hard carbon is very attractive due to its high capacity and low cost.  However, hard carbon anodes often suffer a low first-cycle coulombic efficiency and fast capacity fading.  In this study, we discover that doping graphene oxide into sucrose, the precursor for hard carbon, can effectively reduce the sp. surface area of hard carbon to as low as 5.4 m2/g.  We further show that such doping can effectively prevent foaming during caramelization of sucrose and extend the pyrolysis burnoff of sucrose caramel over a wider temp. range.  The obtained low-surface-area hard carbon greatly improves the first-cycle coulombic efficiency from 74% to 83% and delivers a very stable cycle life with 95% of capacity retention after 200 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqaHV_SLIfobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilPb0BaL14_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXks1KlsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=4b387ca5b76e59789c78130fa5560be4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA05118E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of High Performance Hard Carbon Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of high performance hard carbon anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Ning; Liu, Huan; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20560-20566</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A highly reversible, resource-abundant and low-cost anode is indispensable to the future success of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) in large-scale energy storage application.  The authors report the facile synthesis of a biomass-derived hard carbon for SIBs by 1-step pyrolysis of shaddock peel under an inert atm. without activation or any further treatments.  The pyrolytic carbon shows very high reversible sodium storage capacities up to 430.5 mA h/g at a c.d. of 30 mA/g and superior cycling stability with only 2.5% capacity loss over 200 charge-discharge cycles.  The high capacity and excellent cycle performance, combined with the facile synthesis procedure make it a promising anode material for practical SIBs.  The good Na-ion storage property of the shaddock peel-derived pyrolytic carbon is attributed to its unique honeycomb-like morphol. with a shortened distance for Na-ion diffusion, and the large interlayer distance which is available for sodium insertion/extn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUZb0nR_lduLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilPb0BaL14_Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVegtr7O&amp;md5=32487f69bba862d984793316e10ff8e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201701835"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Q.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2 polymorphs in 'rocking-chair' Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aravindan, Vanchiappan; Lee, Yun-Sung; Yazami, Rachid; Madhavi, Srinivasan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">345-351</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This review describes the overall research activities focused on developing high-performance Li-ion batteries (LIBs) fabricated with various TiO2 polymorphs as insertion anodes.  Although several polymorphs of TiO2 have been reported, only the anatase, rutile, bronze, and brookite phases have proven promising.  The bronze phase's lower insertion potential, high reversibility and high current performance makes it an attractive candidate for constructing high power and high energy d. Li-ion power packs.  In addn., the bronze phase exhibits superior performance over the conventional, commercialized spinel Li4Ti5O12 anodes when coupled with the olivine phase LiFePO4.  This exceptional behavior of the bronze phase opens new avenues for the development of high power LIBs capable of powering zero emission transportation and grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLQhs3JFpjc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFu-T0FI6Djg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjvVyhtbk%253D&amp;md5=eca06de04b707546fd8d67b86a9e25a5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201600845"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">As the delegate of tunnel structure Na titanates, Na2Ti6O13 nanorods with dominant large interlayer spacing exposed facet are prepd.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Silicon/Mesoporous Carbon/Crystalline TiO2 Nanoparticles for Highly Stable Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Wang, Yunxiao; Wang, Lianjun; Jiang, Wan; Chou, Shu-Lei; Dou, Shi Xue; Liu, Hua Kun; Yang, Jianping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A core-shell-shell heterostructure of Si nanoparticles as the core with mesoporous carbon and cryst. TiO2 as the double shells (Si@C@TiO2) is utilized as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, which could successfully tackle the vital setbacks of Si anode materials, in terms of intrinsic low cond., unstable solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) films, and serious vol. variations.  Combined with the high theor. capacity of the Si core (4200 mA h g-1), the double shells can perfectly avoid direct contact of Si with electrolyte, leading to stable SEI films and enhanced Coulombic efficiency.  On the other hand, the carbon inner shell is effective at improving the overall cond. of the Si-based electrode; the TiO2 outer shell is expected to serve as a rigid layer to achieve high structural stability and integrity of the core-shell-shell structure.  As a result, the elaborate Si@C@TiO2 core-shell-shell nanoparticles are proven to show excellent Li storage properties.  It delivers high reversible capacity of 1726 mA h g-1 over 100 cycles, with outstanding cyclability of 1010 mA h g-1 even after 710 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrej2OFRLKM0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFu-T0FI6Djg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslCksbvI&amp;md5=59a1dd6a37d99bffbc113f9cf66381ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700523"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, J.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li and Na Diffusion in TiO2 from Quantum Chemical Theory versus Electrochemical Experiment</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lunell, Sten; Stashans, Arvids; Ojamaee, Lars; Lindstroem, Henrik; Hagfeldt, Anders</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Diffusion of Li and Na ions in TiO2, anatase, has been studied using theor. (quantum chem. ab initio periodic Hartree-Fock and a modified semiempirical INDO) as well as electrochem. (chronocoulometry) methods.  On the basis of the theor. calcns., the geometry of equil. and transition states for the impurities as well as the cryst. framework are analyzed and discussed.  The calcd. activation energies for Li+ and Na+ diffusion were found to be only slightly higher than 0.5 eV by both theor. methods.  The agreement of either theor. method with the electrochem. expts., 0.60 and 0.52 eV for Li+ and Na+, resp., is also remarkably good.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoZSQsZNm6fE7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh25w4ydXrFfg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2sXltFShsro%253D&amp;md5=813837569dfc6e90800d44924d1f8caf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b02348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Su, D.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase TiO2: Better Anode Material Than Amorphous and Rutile Phases of TiO2 for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Dawei; Dou, Shixue; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6022-6029</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous TiO2@C nanospheres were synthesized via a template approach.  After being sintered under different conditions, two types of polyphase TiO2 hollow nanospheres were obtained.  The electrochem. properties of the amorphous TiO2 nanospheres and the TiO2 hollow nanospheres with different phases were characterized as anodes for the Na-ion batteries.  It was found that all the samples demonstrated excellent cyclability, which was sustainable for hundreds of cycles with little capacity fading, although the anatase TiO2 presented a capability that was better than that of the mixed anatase/rutile TiO2 or the amorphous TiO2@C.  Through crystallog. anal., it was revealed that the anatase TiO2 crystal structure supplies two-dimensional diffusion paths for Na-ion intercalation and more accommodation sites.  D. functional theory calcns. indicated lower energy barriers for the insertion of Na+ into anatase TiO2.  Therefore, anatase TiO2 hollow nanospheres show excellent high-rate performance.  Through ex situ field emission SEM, it was revealed that the TiO2 hollow nanosphere architecture can be maintained for hundreds of cycles, which is the main reason for its superior cyclability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGohsYIdXKQ-ZLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNYPuF-zYPFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlSmtLvO&amp;md5=4e702bfdd0ada6787dd1d1f2bf052430</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b03757"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiong, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun TiO2/C Nanofibers As a High-Capacity and Cycle-Stable Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Ya; Qian, Jiangfeng; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16684-16689</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanosized TiO2 is now actively developed as a low-cost and potentially high capacity anode material of Na-ion batteries, but its poor capacity utilization and insufficient cyclability remains an obstacle for battery applications.  To overcome these drawbacks, electrospun TiO2/C nanofibers are synthesized, where anatase TiO2 nanocrystals with a diam. of ∼12 nm were densely embedded in the conductive carbon fibers, thus preventing them from aggregating and attacking by electrolyte.  Due to its abundant active surfaces of well-dispersed TiO2 nanocrytals and high electronic cond. of the carbon matrix, the TiO2/C anode shows a high redox capacity of ∼302.4 mA h g-1 and a high-rate capability of 164.9 mAh g-1 at a very high current of 2000 mA g-1.  More significantly, this TiO2/C anode can be cycled with nearly 100% capacity retention over 1000 cycles, showing a sufficiently long cycle life for battery applications.  The nanofibrous architecture of the TiO2/C composite and its superior electrochem. performance may provide new insights for development of better host materials for practical Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCpHAcLSLQBbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNYPuF-zYPFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpvFyksbs%253D&amp;md5=8d1d90e0be7950d635c188eadb00aaed</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b03270"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boron-Doped Anatase TiO2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Baofeng; Zhao, Fei; Du, Guodong; Porter, Spencer; Liu, Yong; Zhang, Peng; Cheng, Zhenxiang; Liu, Hua Kun; Huang, Zhenguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16009-16015</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pristine and boron-doped anatase TiO2 were prepd. via a facile sol-gel method and the hydrothermal method for application as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The sol-gel method leads to agglomerated TiO2, whereas the hydrothermal method is conducive to the formation of highly cryst. and discrete nanoparticles.  The structure, morphol., and electrochem. properties were studied.  The crystal size of TiO2 with boron doping is smaller than that of the nondoped crystals, which indicates that the addn. of boron can inhibit the crystal growth.  The electrochem. measurements demonstrated that the reversible capacity of the B-doped TiO2 is higher than that for the pristine sample.  B-doping also effectively enhances the rate performance.  The capacity of the B-doped TiO2 could reach 150 mAh/g at the high current rate of 2C and the capacity decay is only about 8 mAh/g over 400 cycles.  The remarkable performance could be attributed to the lattice expansion resulting from B doping and the shortened Li+ diffusion distance due to the nanosize.  These results indicate that B-doped TiO2 can be a good candidate for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqa4lL9nW9zibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljNYPuF-zYPFA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpt1aruro%253D&amp;md5=d6d050542c7f7e1438212730be56e3df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b02724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles in Situ Growth on Graphene Hybrid as Superior Anode Material for Sodium/Lithium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall TiO2 Nanoparticles in Situ Growth on Graphene Hybrid as Superior Anode Material for Sodium/Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huiqiao; Cao, Kangzhe; Xu, Xiaohong; Jiao, Lifang; Wang, Yijing; Yuan, Huatang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To inhibit the aggregation of TiO2 nanoparticles and to improve the electrochem. kinetics of TiO2 electrode, a hybrid material of ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles in situ grown on rGO nanosheets was obtained by ultrasonic and reflux methods.  The size of the TiO2 particles was controlled ∼10 nm, and these particles were evenly distributed across the rGO nanosheets.  When used for the anode of a Na ion battery, the electrochem. performance of this hybrid TiO2@rGO was much improved.  A capacity of 186.6 mA h g-1 was obtained after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, and 112.2 mA h g-1 could be maintained at 1.0 A g-1, showing a high capacity and good rate capability.  From the anal. of cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS), the achieved excellent electrochem. performance was mainly attributed to the synergetic effect of well-dispersed ultra-small TiO2 nanoparticles and conductive graphene network and the improved electrochem. kinetics.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Shape-Controlled TiO2 Nanocrystals for Na-Ion Battery Electrodes: The Role of Different Exposed Crystal Facets on the Electrochemical Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Longoni, Gianluca; Pena Cabrera, Rosita Lissette; Polizzi, Stefano; D'Arienzo, Massimiliano; Mari, Claudio Maria; Cui, Yi; Ruffo, Riccardo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">992-1000</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium-ion batteries are becoming a viable alternative to lithium-based technol. in energy storage strategies, due to the wide abundance of sodium raw material.  In the past decade, this has generated a boom of research interest in such systems.  Notwithstanding the large no. of research papers concerning sodium-ion battery electrodes, the development of a low-cost, well-performing anode material remains the largest obstacle to overcome.  Although the well-known anatase, one of the allotropic forms of natural TiO2, was recently proposed for such applications, the material generally suffers from reduced cyclability and limited power, due to kinetic drawbacks and to its poor charge transport properties.  A systematic approach in the morphol. tuning of the anatase nanocrystals is needed, to optimize its structural features toward the electrochem. properties and to promote the material interaction with the conductive network and the electrolyte.  Aiming to face with these issues, a fine tuning was obtained of the nanoparticle morphol. and to expose the most favorable nanocrystal facets to the electrolyte and to the conductive wrapping agent (graphene), thus overcoming the intrinsic limits of anatase transport properties.  The result is a TiO2-based composite electrode able to deliver an outstandingly stability over cycles (150 mA h g-1 for more than 600 cycles in the 1.5-0.1 V potential range) never achieved with such a low content of carbonaceous substrate (5%).  Moreover, it has been demonstrated for the first time that these outstanding performances are not simply related to the overall surface area of the different morphologies but have to be directly related to the peculiar surface characteristics of the crystals.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWUF1Ch-SrS7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhilTZ3-N5BMQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced electrochemical properties of TiO2(B) nanoribbons using the styrene butadiene rubber and sodium carboxyl methyl cellulose water binder</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Xiao; Zhang, Yongquan; Zhu, Kai; Gao, Yu; Zhang, Dong; Chen, Gang; Wang, Chunzhong; Wei, Yingjin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">246</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">TiO2(B) anode for Li-ion batteries is prepd. by the hydrothermal method.  Styrene butadiene rubber and Na carboxyl Me cellulose (SBR/CMC) and polyvinylidene fluoride (PVdF) binders are used to prep. the TiO2(B) electrodes.  Scanning electron microscope and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy show that the electrode prepd. with SBR/CMC has better electrode maintainability and electrochem. kinetics which result in better electrochem. performance.  The optimized SBR/CMC binder content probably is at 12-15%.  The 1 M LiPF6 electrolyte dissolved in EC:DMC = 3:7 is more suitable for the TiO2(B) electrode.  Using this suggested binder content and electrolyte, the TiO2(B) material exhibits superior capacity retention and rate capability.  Even at the 10 C rate, the material still shows a discharge capacity of 142.5 mA-h g-1 which keeps well after 800 cycles.  Based on this work, SBR/CMC is a promising binder for the TiO2(B) anode which provides better electrochem. performance and is cheaper and more environmentally friendly than PVdF.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_5SWs0CxbO7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhilTZ3-N5BMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFCqtLjM&amp;md5=1987743dce20133f883ee4ce24c7c01d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee22292b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Z.-J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shimomura, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Murase, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yui, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Capacity Si–graphite Composite Electrodes with a Self-Formed Porous Structure by a Partially Neutralized Polyacrylate for Li-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity Si-graphite composite electrodes with a self-formed porous structure by a partially neutralized polyacrylate for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Zhen-Ji; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Shimomura, Keiji; Murase, Masahiro; Yui, Hiroharu; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9014-9020</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NaOH-neutralized poly(acrylic acid) is examd. as a binder for Si-based neg. electrodes in rechargeable Li-ion batteries.  To better understand the influence of polymer binder characteristics, the impact of neutralization degree (ND) of poly(acrylic acid) (PAH) on electrode performance of a Si-graphite composite is studied.  The electrode performance of the Si-based composites is remarkably improved by appropriate neutralization of PAH because the NDs highly influence rheol. properties of a slurry and thus the electrode morphol., such as porosity.  It is found that 80% neutralized PAH provides the moderate porous structure inside the composite electrode with 10 wt% binder content because of a unique rheol. property during the drying process after casting the slurry onto a current collector.  The self-formed porous structure by the partially neutralized PAH is beneficial to buffer vol. expansion caused by lithiation of Si.  Therefore, an excellent capacity retention for a 100 cycle test with a high reversible capacity of approx. 1000 mA h g-1 is achieved with the 80% neutralized PAH as a binder for Si-based composite electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpi61_sqKRbprVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhilTZ3-N5BMQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xhtlyqs7vJ&amp;md5=cb5b9f17dc1fe9a8951b4b4ec2e05b8d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201201568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Koo, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cho, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, K.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Highly Cross-Linked Polymeric Binder for High-Performance Silicon Negative Electrodes in Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Koo, Bonjae; Kim, Hyunjung; Cho, Younghyun; Lee, Kyu Tae; Choi, Nam-Soon; Cho, Jaephil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We present an innovative thermally cured polymeric binder as a technol. soln. for lithium-ion batteries with silicon-based anodes.  Nanosized silicon powder with a tree-dimensionally interconnected network of poly(acrylic acid) and sodium CM-cellulose as binder exhibits a high reversible capacity of &gt;2000 mA-h/g after 100 cycles at 30° and maintains superior capacity of 1500 mA-h/g for the high c.d. of 30 A/g at 60°.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Major Constituent of Brown Algae for Use in High-Capacity Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kovalenko, Igor; Zdyrko, Bogdan; Magasinski, Alexandre; Hertzberg, Benjamin; Milicev, Zoran; Burtovyy, Ruslan; Luzinov, Igor; Yushin, Gleb</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The identification of similarities in the material requirements for applications of interest and those of living organisms provides opportunities to use renewable natural resources to develop better materials and design better devices.  In the authors' work, the authors harness this strategy to build high-capacity Si nanopowder-based Li-ion batteries with improved performance characteristics.  Si offers more than one order of magnitude higher capacity than graphite, but it exhibits dramatic vol. changes during electrochem. alloying and de-alloying with Li, which typically leads to rapid anode degrdn.  Mixing Si nanopowder with alginate, a natural polysaccharide extd. from brown algae, yields a stable battery anode possessing reversible capacity eight times higher than that of the state-of-the-art graphitic anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGom1H4XyLyXZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEB3m0JNBeOQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1Gms7%252FO&amp;md5=dcfc4f4e89e738e37384c6bf58685cc8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1007/s10811-009-9432-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fenoradosoa, T.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extraction and characterization of an alginate from the brown seaweed Sargassum turbinarioides Grunow</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fenoradosoa, Taratra Andree; Ali, Ghina; Delattre, Cedric; Laroche, Celine; Petit, Emmanuel; Wadouachi, Anne; Michaud, Philippe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Phycology</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Matrix polysaccharide from the brown algae Sargassum turbinarioides collected in the coastal waters of Nosy Be (Madagascar) in the Indian Ocean was isolated and its structure was studied by 1H-NMR spectroscopy, FT-IR, SEC-MALLS and HPAEC.  An alginate with a mol. wt. of 5.528 × 105 g mol-1 was identified as sole polysaccharide.  Values of the M/G ratio, F GG, F MM and F GM (or F GM) blocks were measured at resp. 0.94, 0.39, 0.36 and 0.25 and compared with those of alginates from other Sargassum species.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of reduced graphene on crystallization behavior, thermal conductivity and tribological properties of poly(vinylidene fluoride)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Peng; Fan, Jingbo; Jing, Maoxiang; Zhu, Lin; Shen, Xiangqian; Pan, Tiezheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Composite Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The reduced graphene/poly(vinylidene fluoride) nanocomposite films were prepd. by the soln. casting-thermal redn. process using graphene oxide and poly(vinylidene fluoride) resin.  The results show that with the presence of reduced graphene nano sheets in the nanocomposite, the structure of poly(vinylidene fluoride) tends to transform from α- to β-phase and the β-phase fraction and its crystallinity are largely affected by the reduced graphene content.  The thermal cond. of poly(vinylidene fluoride) can be effectively improved by the reduced graphene nano sheets introduction and when the reduced graphene content increased to about 10.0 wt%, it is about two times higher than the pure poly(vinylidene fluoride), due to the excellent thermal cond. of reduced graphene and formation of thermal conductive networks.  With comparison of the pure poly(vinylidene fluoride), the reduced graphene/poly(vinylidene fluoride) nanocomposite films show a better tribol. property at a low reduced graphene content (below 4.0 wt%), mainly owing to the lubricant and heat spreading effects of reduced graphene nano sheets.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase Titania Nanorods as an Intercalation Anode Material for Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Ki-Tae; Ali, Ghulam; Chung, Kyung Yoon; Yoon, Chong Seung; Yashiro, Hitoshi; Sun, Yang-Kook; Lu, Jun; Amine, Khalil; Myung, Seung-Taek</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">416-422</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. activity of anatase TiO2 nanorods in a Na cell.  The anatase TiO2 nanorods were synthesized by a hydrothermal method, and their surfaces were coated by carbon to improve the elec. cond. by carbonization of pitch at 700° for 2 h in Ar flow.  The resulting structure does not change before and after the carbon coating, as confirmed by x-ray diffraction.  Transmission electron microscopy images confirm the presence of a carbon coating on the anatase TiO2 nanorods.  In cell tests, anodes of bare and carbon-coated anatase TiO2 nanorods exhibit stable cycling performance and attain a capacity of about 172 and 193 mA-h/g on the first charge, resp., in the voltage range of 0-3 V.  With the help of the conductive carbon layers, the carbon-coated anatase TiO2 delivers more capacity at high rates, 104 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g), 82 mA-h/g at the 30C rate (10 A/g), and 53 mA-h/g at the 100C rate (33 A g-1).  By contrast, the anode of bare anatase TiO2 nanorods delivers only about 38 mA-h/g at the 10C rate (3.3 A/g).  The excellent cyclability and high-rate capability are the result of a Na+ insertion and extn. reaction into the host structure coupled with Ti4+/3+ redox reaction, as shown by x-ray absorption spectroscopy.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpadjcIpWM-W7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhfjHdYloCmOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXktlGhsA%253D%253D&amp;md5=4bc3a520e6f654a82cbee3b778eef0e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/am501772a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oh, S.-M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hwang, J.-Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yoon, C.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anatase TiO2 nanocubes for fast and durable sodium ion battery anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Xuming; Wang, Chao; Yang, Yingchang; Zhang, Yan; Jia, Xinnan; Chen, Jun; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the aim of advancing anatase TiO2 anodes for Na ion batteries, cryst. TiO2 nanocubes were employed and they delivered a gradually increasing capacity during the initial cycles, termed as an activation process.  The no. of necessary discharge-charge loops for total activation is dependent on the galvanostatic c.d. (∼20 cycles at 0.2 C, or 90 cycles at 1 C).  A percentage of Ti3+ was detected after the activation, indicating an amt. of irreversibly trapped Na ions in the lattice.  After the activation process, an excellent rate capability and outstanding cycling stability were presented.  The reversible capacity reached 174, 132, and 108 mA h g-1 at rates of 1 C, 5 C, and 10 C, resp.  The capacity was sustained with a loss of &lt;10% after 1000 discharge-charge cycles at a rate of 2 C or 10 C.  The superior battery performance achieved by the nanocubes is related to the encircled {100} facets that are more favorable for Na ion attachment compared to the {001} and {101} facets, as supported by 1st-principles calcns.  From this work the authors can see the feasibility of optimizing electrode materials via rational surface structure construction based on theor. calcns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpebO59ke4jqbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWOMLt_YnKWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvFGjsrw%253D&amp;md5=a5ab3c8c5cb9855d41e67b06bcde30de</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7929"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6929</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGrV7K8Tq5mLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWOMLt_YnKWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2lurzK&amp;md5=99303fd99ef59044874690750282067a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b00633"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, L.
